## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task seeks the constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature in a material. Temperature typically modifies elastic moduli and flow stress through thermal softening, while strain determines stress through elastic/plastic hardening laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at constant temperature)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (linear elasticity with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress with thermal expansion strain subtracted)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (rational): sigma = c0 * epsilon * c1 / (c1 + T) (modulus decreasing with temperature via rational form)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Ramberg-Osgood style)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T) (power-law hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (modulus with Arrhenius-type temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with cross-term)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (yield + hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Hyperelastic (Neo-Hookean type): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) * (c2 - c3 * T) (nonlinear elasticity with thermal effects)
- Arrhenius flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * c3 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Combined model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T + c3 * T**2) (modulus as quadratic function of temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) representing decreasing modulus/strength with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Thermally activated processes → exp(-c/T) or exp(c/T) Arrhenius factors when deformation is diffusion-controlled
- Elastic-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth transition combining linear (c*epsilon) at small strain with power-law (epsilon**c) at large strain
- Multiplicative decomposition of thermal and mechanical effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable strain and temperature contributions
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → E(T) often linear (c0 - c1*T) or follows polynomial in T, multiplying strain
- Strain-temperature coupling → Cross-terms epsilon*T indicate that hardening rate changes with temperature
- Negative temperature exponents → T**(-c) or inverse-T terms suggest creep or diffusion-dominated regimes at high temperature
